4.    Institutional Arraiwements and Implementation Procedures
The Deputy Commissioner's (DC) office in each District will acquire the land, acting on behalf of
LGED as the requiring body. To support the DCs, and to ensure timely implementation in accordance with
the LAAP, LGED will take a pro-active role. As a rural development agency with a social as well as
technical perspective, and with offices in every District and Thana, LGED is well-placed to do this. The
key LGED actors will be the District XENs, the Thana Engineers, and the Community Organisers at thana
level. They will be supported by the PIO, whose incremental staffing includes a Sociologist in each of the
14 project Districts, and the Design, Supervision and Monitoring Consultants (DSMC), whose staffing
includes two national Land Acquisition Field Advisers. The DSMC advisers will work full-time on land
acquisition and will set up and operate the monitoring system. The incremental staffing also includes a
Socio-Economist in PIO headquarters in Dhaka to work on land acquisition and participation aspects, and
a Sociologist in LGED headquarters who, inter-alia, will develop LGED land acquisition practices. Union
Parishads will be involved in the information campaign and grievance redressal procedure.
This is the first Bank-financed project in Bangladesh where land acquisition procedures
conforming to OD 4.30 will involve only government machinery, without availing of NGO support. As
such it represents a major step forward in the institutionalization of land acquisition procedures.
The implementation strategy allows ample time for land acquisition so that, for each year of full
implementation of FRB works, it can be completed prior to the planned start of construction. The annual
implementation schedule (Figure 1) allows a 13 month period for land acquisition up to the end of the three
month eviction period, so that land is available for physical occupation by LGED prior to completion of
road construction contract tendering. The schedule allows some slack for delays in the process.
At the time of submission of the case to the DC, the DSMC will make a photographic record of the
road, to document the pre-existence of buildings and trees on the alignment, as one measure to discourage
'fraudulent' compensation claims. A Joint On-Site Inventory and Verification will be carried out, involving
the LAO, LGED, the DSMC Field Adviser, and the PAPs. This will define and record the PAPs, the assets
to be acquired, the losses, and any disputes over ownership of assets. People within the vicinity of the road
will be informed in advance of the exercise. This inventory and verification will form the basis for all
subsequent stages of the land acquisition, and for monitoring.
The DSMC Field Adviser and the PIO will undertake a market survey in the area of each road to
assess the values of agricultural, homestead and developed commercial land; of buildings; and of standing
trees and perennial crops. LGED and the P10 will then negotiate with the DC with the aim of reaching
agreement on assessed values that reflect full market values. If such agreement is not reached, and if the
DC's assessed values are lower than LGED's market values, LGED will make additional, 'top up' payments
directly to PAPs. Payment of compensation to PAPs will be made at Union headquarters, in order to avoid
the problems that PAPs often face in travelling long distances to obtain small compensation amounts.
LGED will assist the DC in arrangements to make these payments. There will be some cases, where
ownership of assets is unresolved, or where legal disputes are in process, that will not be completed prior to
physical occupation of the land.

5.    Information, Assistance and Grievance Procedures
LGED will disseminate information about the land acquisition and compensation process. The
information campaign in the vicinity of each road, which will involve the Union Parishad and will include
the posting of notices and the distribution of leaflets, will start when the case is submitted to the DC.
LGED will inform people that it is intended to acquire land. It will advise them of the procedures to be
adopted and of the assets and losses that will be compensated (and of those that will not be compensated);
of the persons entitled to compensation; of their rights and the steps that they should take to protect those
rights; and of the assistance available from LGED to resolve problems and grievamces. During the Joint
On-Site Inventory and Verification PAPs will again be advised of the procedures and of the support
available from LGED. After the issue of Notice No.7, PAPs will be informed of compensation payments
arrangements. At the time payments are made, PAPs will be informed of the time they have to vacate the
land, and of the entitlement to salvage certain assets.
LGED will assist PAPs to resolve queries and redress grievances. The grievance redressal
procedure will operate through a committee in each Thana chaired by the Thana Engineer and comprising
the District Sociologist and a member of the Union Parishad, which will meet regularly (about twice per
month) at advertised times at the TE's office, when PAPs can formally present and discuss their queries and
grievances. PAPs can ask a Union Parishad member to assist them. This committee will resolve some
matters, and will determine that certain grievances are not legitimate. Where necessary, the committee will
ask the District Sociologist, assisted by the DSMC Field Adviser, to follow-up. This may involve field
investigations on-site with the PAP and his/her Union Parishad representative. The committee will then
meet again with the PAP to review the findings of the investigation. For legitimate grievances which the
committee is unable to resolve, a report will be submitted to the XEN, who will take further steps to resolve
the grievance and if necessary will submit a formal request to the DC to consider the matter. The Thana
Engineer will maintain a register of all queries and grievances presented to the committee, and of the
actions taken and decisions made. This grievance procedure will not replace the existing legal appeal
process, but will minimise the number of cases that reach the stage of legal action and will expedite the
resolution of problems.
6.    Monitoring and Reporting Procedure
The DSM consultants, working with the PIO Sociologist, will monitor the progress and
performance of land acquisition. The project Annual Plan of Operations (APO) will include targets for
objectively verifiable indicators of progress of land acquisition. Monitoring and reporting will be based on
comparison of actual progress on each road with these targets. Key progress indicators will be:
*      Date of submission of land acquisition case to DC
*     Date of completion of land market survey
*     Number of plots acquired
The Joint On-Site Inventory and Verification will form the basis for monitoring performance. A
computerised data-base will be set up for each road to record information for each identified PAP. It will
then be used to track the performance of land acquisition as implementation proceeds. Performance will be
monitored in terms of



195                                 Annex 3.8
Page 9 of 10
*     Numbers of PAPs
*     Characteristics of PAPs
*     Nature and level of impact
*     Value of compensation due to PAPs
*      Status of payment of compensation to PAPs
*     Progress of owners of homestead land, business proprietors, uthulis and squatters in re-
location
*     Resolution of grievances
*     Numbers of legally disputed and other unresolved cases
*     Compliance with the eviction period
The project will report twice per year on progress and performance. This will be incorporated into
the relevant project quarterly progress reports. The DSMC, as part of their input to the SEM&E activities,
and in collaboration with PIO and LGED SEM&E staff, will undertake broader studies of the impact of
land acquisition on affected persons. The IDA and SDC will review the progress and performance by
LGED of land acquisition as part of project supervision. About once per year, as required by IDA/SDC, an
independent review of compliance by LGED of the policies set out in the LAAP will be carried out.
7.    Budget
The costs of land acquisition have been estimated using the data on quantities from the Preliminary
Inventory Survey, and the findings from the LAA on market values of assets. Table 3 details the direct cost
by District for acquisition of land, buildings and trees. The total estimated cost is Taka 150.8 million
(US$3.77 million), or 7.3% of total FRB improvement and upgrading costs. The total cost is based on
broad estimates of unit values of assets, and given this degree of uncertainty a 25% physical contingency
has been included for land acquisition. Land acquisition will be 100% GOB financed.
Table 3 also details the overhead and administrative costs of implementing the land acquisition
process in accordance with the LAAP. The estimated cost is Taka 16.1 million (US$0.4 million), about
11% of the direct cost of land acquisition. In addition, some permanent LGED District and Thana staff will
spend time on land acquisition matters. The total direct, overhead and administrative cost of land
acquisition, including physical and price contingencies, is estimated at Taka 219.3 million (US$5.5
million).

BANGLADESH
SECOND RURAL ROADS AND MARKETS IMPROVEMENT AND MAINTENANCE PROJECT
SECTORAL ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT: SUMMARY'
1.    Introduction
The project is not expected to have a major impact on the physical or ecological environment. No new
road alignments are involved. The proposed works are improvement, upgrading and maintenance of
existing roads and will have positive environmental impacts - the provision of drainage structures will
reduce waterlogging; bitumen surfacing will eliminate the dust hazard; the hard shoulders will improve
safety; road safety measures will be applied to reduce congestion and accidents; and trees will be
planted on the embankment slopes of all project roads, more than compensating for tree felling during
construction. The physical environment, health standards and quality of life in the markets and ghats
will be improved through provision of free-draining paved areas, hygienic latrines, garbage disposal
facilities and potable water supplies. Bio-gas generators will be installed at markets to process solid
waste. The use of labour-intensive construction and maintenance methods, and of local materials
provides a sound environmental approach, and the use of environmentally-friendly construction
materials will be promoted, including bitumen emulsion which eliminates the need for firewood to heat
bitumen. The environmental category for this project is Category B.
LGED has carried out an environmental impact study with assistance from the preparation consultants,
based on LGED environmental guidelines, to identify all positive and negative project impacts and
define the mitigation measures. This has been used to prepare a Sectoral Enviromnental Assessment.
2.    Measures to Mitigate Negative Environmental Impacts of Road Improvements
The potential negative impacts are primarily related to the FRB works. Table 1 details these - classified
as High, Medium and Low risk - the proposed mitigation measures, and responsibilities for those
measures, which will be applied to design, contracting, supervision, and operation of roads.
Design
Environmental considerations are incorporated into the technical design standards. Alignments will be
adjusted to avoid cultural features. Sufficient structures will be provided, with adequate openings, to
maintain natural drainage and navigability of channels - locations and sizes of structures will be
determined based on field surveys, consultations with local people, and hydrological investigations.
All improved embankments will be above the high flood level, constructed from suitable soil and
mechanically compacted, with rigorous testing. Cambers and embankment slopes are specified to shed
surface water and maintain soil stability, and erosion protection measures will be applied where
necessary. All roads will be constructed with hard shoulders on each side of the pavement, and road
safety signs and warning markers will be installed. Road safety measures will be incorporated at
junctions, blackspots and adjacent to markets. Four project roads are within wildlife sanctuaries
(Bhawal, Bil Bhatia and Chalan Beel) but project activities will not disturb the critical natural habitats.
' Details are in the Project file, in Document entitled "Sectoral Environmental Assessment for RRMIMP-2"



Annex 3.9
198                                  Page 2 of 6
Contracting
The contract documents incorporate environmental considerations. They detail the design standards and
the procedures for testing of soil and compaction. They define the responsibilities of, and the
procedures that will be adopted by, contractors for location and operation of site camps; location,
excavation and reinstatement of borrow pits; temporary diversion of water channels and protection of
unstable embankments; haulage of materials; storage and handling of materials; disposal of waste; and
provision of road diversions and temporary traffic safety measures during construction.
Supervision
The compliance of contractors with the environmental requirements will be supervised by LGED, with
the assistance of the DSM consultants. Soil and compaction testing will be a key element of
supervision. LGED supervision staff will be trained in supervision of environmental aspects of
construction works. Attention will be paid to mitigating negative impacts of disposal of waste
materials, and the project will develop standards and indicators to monitor this. Trees will be planted
on road embankment slopes, except on the inside of curves.
Operation
Routine maintenance will be applied to all project roads, including caretaking of the trees. This will
mitigate against longer-term negative environmental impacts and sustain the environmental benefits.
Maintenance of the smooth road surfaces will encourage the use of non-motorised transport (NMT).
The pilot program to improve NMT will also promote the use of environmentally sound vehicles. The
extension of routine and periodic maintenance to non-project roads will enhance the environment.
Local government bodies will be encouraged to control development adjacent to the roads.
3.     Measures to Mitigate Negative Environmental Impacts of Market and Ghat Improvements
The environmental impacts of market and ghat improvements will be predominantly positive. Users
will participate in the detailed design of the improvements to ensure that the numbers and types of
facilities - including latrines and potable water supplies - meet local requirements. The main potential
negative impact is if inadequate provision is made for the drainage and disposal of surface and waste
water. The following measures will be taken to mitigate against this:
*     The DSM consultants will establish the design levels of the market and ghat paved areas to
ensure that they are free-draining. Internal drains, designed for easy cleaning, will be provided
in the market/ghat areas. Adequate, safe drain outfalls will be designed to ensure that there is
no drainage congestion.
*     LGED and the DSM consultants will supervise construction works to ensure that the paved
areas are built to the design levels and grades, and with the necessary outfalls. The project will
train LGED staff in the supervision of market and ghat construction.
*     The project will develop the capability of the Market and Ghat Management Committees to
maintain the markets and ghats. Improved procedures for cleaning the markets, maintaining
free-drainage and disposing of garbage will be introduced.



Annex 3.9
199                                Page 3 of 6
Following the pilot initiative taken by LGED under the RDP-6 project, bio-gas generators will be
installed in improved markets to process human, animal and vegetable waste to produce gas and
compost. Management Conmnittees will be trained in the operation of the generators.
4.    Monitoring
Monitoring of short-term negative environmental impacts during the construction phase will be
integrated into the supervision of the works. Longer-term environmental impacts of road improvement
works will be monitored in four ways:
*     Monitoring of compliance with design standards and specifications will be part of the
supervision of construction works.
The regular inspection of roads for the planning and implementation of maintenance will
generate data on their condition in respect of erosion, surface condition, state of tree
plantations, blockage of drainage structures and condition of road signs and markings.
Project SEM&E activities will include regular traffic counts on improved roads, generating
data to monitor changes in the levels of motorised and non-motorised traffic.
*     Special surveys will be carried out of a sample of improved roads to monitor the extent to
which any of the following negative impacts are occurring:
-     turbidity of roadside water;
-     drainage congestion during floods;
-     interference with boat communications;
-     pollution of surface and ground water;
-     disruption of fish migration and breeding;
-     encroachment of commercial and residential activities.
*     Monitoring of the environmental situation of improved markets and ghats will be incorporated
into monitoring of the effectiveness of project actions to increase the capability of Market and
Ghat Management Committees.
The project will report annually on the environmental impact of its activities, and on the effectiveness
of avoidance, mitigation and enhancement measures. The PIO staffing includes a full-time
Environmental Engineer who will have direct responsibility for monitoring and reporting.
5.    Institutional Strengthening
LGED has a program to address environmental issues at the planning and design stages. It has
guidelines on environmental assessment and two in-house environmental specialists. The guidelines are
now being revised. LGED also has an environmental training program for XENs.
The National Environmental Management Action Plan (NEMAP) will provide the national policy
framework on environmental management within which LGED will operate in future. LGED would
benefit from an in-house Environmental Unit to be responsible for environmental planning and
management. The LGED training program on environmental impact assessment should be expanded



200                                  Annex 3.9
Page 4 of 6
and made mandatory for all levels of personnel. Training in environmental matters should be extended
to contractors, and to Union Parishads and Market and Ghat Management Committees.
LGED should develop standard clauses on environmental aspects, similar to those adopted for the
RRMIMP-2, for inclusion in technical specifications and conditions of contract, together with
procedures for monitoring and supervision of mitigation measures during construction. The integration
of environmental concerns into LGED planning procedures, and the increased participation of local
people in all stages of infrastructure development, will enhance LGED's environmental performance.
